</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Harvard–Yale Regatta</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard-Yale_Regatta&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard-Yale Regatta">Harvard-Yale Regatta</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>

<p>The <b>Harvard-Yale Regatta</b> or <b>Yale-Harvard Boat Race</b> (often abbreviated <b>The Race</b>) is an annual <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a> race between the men's heavyweight rowing crews of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>. First contested in 1852, it has been held annually since 1859 except during major wars fought by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The Race is America's oldest <a href="/wiki/College_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="College sports">collegiate athletic</a> competition, pre-dating <a href="/wiki/Harvard-Yale_football_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard-Yale football rivalry">The Game</a> by 23 years. It is sometimes referred to as the "Yale-Harvard" regatta, though most official regatta programs brand it "Harvard-Yale."<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Originally rowed on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Winnipesaukee" title="Lake Winnipesaukee">Lake Winnipesaukee</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, it has since moved to the <a href="/wiki/Thames_River_(Connecticut)" title="Thames River (Connecticut)">Thames River</a>, near <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London, Connecticut</a>. Although other locations for the race have included the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_River" title="Connecticut River">Connecticut River</a> at <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Quinsigamond" title="Lake Quinsigamond">Lake Quinsigamond</a> at <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">Worcester, Massachusetts</a>, the Thames has hosted The Race on all but five occasions since 1878 and both teams have erected permanent training camps on the Thames at <a href="/wiki/Gales_Ferry#The_Ferry" class="mw-redirect" title="Gales Ferry">Gales Ferry</a> for Yale and at Red Top for Harvard.</p>
<p>The race has been exclusively between Yale and Harvard except for 1897 when the race was held as part of a three-boat race with <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> at <a href="/wiki/Poughkeepsie_(city),_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Poughkeepsie (city), New York">Poughkeepsie, New York</a>, where, although it lost to Cornell, Yale was deemed the winner of the Harvard-Yale race.<sup id="cite_ref-USRowing_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USRowing-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-veneziano_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veneziano-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On May 24, 1843, with the arrival of the shell <i>Whitehall</i> in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a>, Yale University founded the first collegiate crew in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Great_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Great-12">[12]</a></sup> A year later, Harvard founded their boat club.<sup id="cite_ref-p224_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p224-13">[13]</a></sup> These boat clubs served primarily a social purpose,<sup id="cite_ref-p224_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p224-13">[13]</a></sup> until Yale's 1852 issuance of a challenge to Harvard "to test the superiority of the oarsmen of the two colleges".<sup id="cite_ref-veneziano_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veneziano-11">[11]</a></sup> The first Harvard–Yale Boat Race—and the first American intercollegiate sporting event—took place on August 3, 1852. In this two-mile (3.2&#160;km) contest, Harvard's <i>Oneida</i> prevailed over Yale's <i>Shawmut</i> by about two lengths, with Yale's <i>Undine</i> finishing third.<sup id="cite_ref-Great_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Great-12">[12]</a></sup> The first place prize was a pair of black walnut, silver-inscribed trophy oars. The trophy oars were awarded to Harvard by General <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce" title="Franklin Pierce">Franklin Pierce</a> who in 1853 became the 14th <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the United States of America">President of the United States of America</a>. Today the 1852 trophy oars are the oldest intercollegiate athletic prize in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The race distance was increased to three miles (4.8&#160;km) for the second rendition in 1855 and to the current four miles (6.4&#160;km) in 1876. The <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">Oxford–Cambridge Boat Race</a> is the only longer side-by-side rowing event in the world, though slower stream makes the Yale–Harvard Race one to three minutes longer.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg/220px-The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg/330px-The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg/440px-The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="478" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Rock_Painted_Crimson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"The Rock" at Bartlett's Cove during the 2010 Harvard–Yale Regatta</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Originally the race was just between the <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity</a> crews but there are now three events: the 2-mile (3.2-km) <a href="/wiki/Freshman" title="Freshman">freshman</a> race, the 3-mile (4.8-km) <a href="/wiki/Junior_varsity" class="mw-redirect" title="Junior varsity">junior varsity</a> race, and the 4-mile (6.4-km) varsity race.<sup id="cite_ref-Yale2009_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yale2009-16">[16]</a></sup> The varsity crews compete for the Sexton Cup, the junior varsity for the F. Valentine Chappell Trophy, and the freshman for the New London Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-Yale2009_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yale2009-16">[16]</a></sup> The Hoyt C. Pease and Robert Chappell Jr. Trophies are awarded to the team that wins the majority of the three races.<sup id="cite_ref-Yale2009_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yale2009-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Typically the day before the freshman, junior varsity and varsity races, there is a two-mile (3.2&#160;km) race between the spares for both crews. These "combination" boats are made up of second freshman boat and third varsity boat rowers (i.e. the "combi" or "combo" race).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The winner of this race gets the James P. Snider Cup, as well as the right to paint its school's colors on the "rock" at Bartlett's Cove for the next day's races.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Currently Harvard leads the varsity series at 95–55, the second varsity (JV) at 75–38, and the freshman series at 72–39–1. Yale holds the upstream course record with its time of 18:35.8 in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The Crimson set the downstream—and Thames River course—mark of 18:22.4 in 1980.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophies">Trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Trophies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(April 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>The Sexton Cup</b> is presented to the winner of the varsity heavyweight race. The trophy is actually a combination of two former rowing trophies: The bottom is the original base of the Sexton Cup, with year-by-year results of race winners, while the upper portion retains the Yale and Harvard seals from the trophy which was awarded to the winner of the (now discontinued) graduate eights race.</p>
<p><b>The F. Valentine Chappell Trophy</b> is presented to the winner of the second varsity heavyweight race. Previously used for a discontinued event in this regatta, it was redesignated in 1983 to be awarded to the victor in the junior varsity contest.</p>
<p><b>The New London Cup</b> is presented to the winner of the freshman race. The city of New London donated this silver award in celebration of its bicentennial and it is inscribed with the Seal of the City of New London and engraved with a ship bearing "Mare Liberium" (Freedom of the Seas). As of 2014, both schools began boating a 3V lineup for this race, rather than an all-freshmen lineup.</p>
<p><b>The Hoyt C. Pease and Robert Chappell Jr. Trophy</b> is presented to the crews who win two or more of the varsity, junior varsity, and freshmen races. This sterling silver bowl was donated by George Pew, Yale Class of 1958, in honor of Pease and Chappell with the inscription: "Named in honor of their great contribution over four decades to the spirit and success of The Boat Race."</p>
<p><b>The James Snider Cup</b> is awarded to the winning crew of the Combination race of the Harvard–Yale Regatta, which is held annually in <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London, Connecticut</a>. The Combination crews are typically composed of rowers from the third varsity and second freshman boats of their respective programs. Traditionally the two crews race a 2-mile (3.2-km) course the day before the Regatta, with the winning crew earning both possession of the Cup and the right to paint the large rock surface south of Bartlett's Cove—typically the most popular viewing spot for the Regatta's main events the next day—with their school's colors.</p>
<p>The James P. Snider Cup was dedicated in honor of James P. "Jamie Sniderman" Snider by the Yale Heavyweight Crew Class of 2005 following the Harvard–Yale Regatta held on June 11, 2005. The cup was donated in honor of Jamie's years of dedicated service to both the Yale Heavyweight Crew and the Yale Crew program as a whole. In 1995 and 1996 Jamie served as an assistant coach of the Yale Women's Crew, leading the 1995 Third Varsity to a 10–4 record. After becoming an assistant with the Men's Heavyweight squad, Jamie led the 1997 Third Varsity Crew to an undefeated season, an Eastern Sprints Gold Medal, and a victory in the Combination Race of the Harvard–Yale Regatta. Jamie's 1999 Combination crew earned the right to paint the rock as well. Currently, Jamie serves as the assistant coach of the Women's Program. In 2006 he led his Third Varsity Four to a third-place finish at the Eastern Sprints, and in 2007, 2008, 2009 he coached the Varsity Four to gold medals at Eastern Sprints and a sixth, sixth and third-place finish at NCAAs.</p>
<p>In addition to coaching Yale crews during the season, Jamie has served as caretaker of <a href="/wiki/Gales_Ferry" class="mw-redirect" title="Gales Ferry">Gales Ferry</a>, the home and training site for the Yale Men's Heavyweight Crew during preparation for the Harvard–Yale Regatta since 1878. He has also served as Director of the Yale University Community Rowing Program since its inception in the summer of 1999. Originally established as a small pilot program, the program has since grown to include over 100 youth participants annually, providing rowing opportunities for organizations such as the National Youth Sports Program, American School for the Deaf, and the Connecticut Special Olympics.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results">Results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Varsity_race">Varsity race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Varsity race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Number of wins: Harvard, 95; Yale, 56</li>
<li>Most consecutive victories: Harvard, 18 (1963–1980)</li>
<li>Course downstream record: Harvard, 1980 – 18&#160;min 22.4&#160;sec; average speed 13.1 miles per hour (21.1&#160;km/h)</li>
<li>Course upstream record: Yale, 2015 – 18&#160;min 35.8&#160;sec; average speed 12.9 miles per hour (20.8&#160;km/h)</li>
<li>Narrowest winning margin: 0.2&#160;sec (Yale, 1914)</li>
<li>Largest winning margin: 1&#160;min 43&#160;sec (Harvard, 1879)</li>
</ul>

<p><b>a.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_anone"><a href="#ref_anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Yale ran into Harvard, which was leading at the turning stake.</p>
<p><b>b.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bnone"><a href="#ref_bnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Yale collided with Harvard.</p>
<p><b>c.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cnone"><a href="#ref_cnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Yale stroke broke oar and dove overboard. Yale still won the race.</p>
<p><b>d.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_dnone"><a href="#ref_dnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Triangular races included Cornell. Cornell won.</p>
<p><b>e.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_enone"><a href="#ref_enone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Yale stroke ejected from shell near three-mile mark.</p>
<p><b>f.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_fnone"><a href="#ref_fnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Shortest race in series history.</p>
<p><b>g.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_gnone"><a href="#ref_gnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Yale's seven seat lost oar and dove overboard at two-mile mark.</p>
<p><b>h.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_gnone"><a href="#ref_gnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> The Harvard boat swamped in rough conditions, and the race was abandoned with Yale ahead. The race was declared to have no official result in January 2017, following an appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_Varsity_race">Junior Varsity race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Junior Varsity race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Number of wins: Harvard, 76; Yale, 39</li>
<li>Most consecutive victories: Harvard, 9 (1967-1975)</li>
<li>Narrowest winning margin: 0.2&#160;sec (Yale, 1952)</li>
<li>Largest winning margin: 1&#160;min 20.5&#160;sec (Yale, 1981)</li>
</ul>

<h3><span id="Freshman_race_(3V_race_as_of_2014)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Freshman_race_.283V_race_as_of_2014.29">Freshman race (3V race as of 2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Freshman race (3V race as of 2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Number of wins: Harvard, 73; Yale, 39 (1 dead heat)</li>
<li>Most consecutive victories: Harvard, 11 (1965-1976)</li>
<li>Narrowest winning margin: 0.4&#160;sec (Yale, 1935)</li>
<li>Largest winning margin: 46&#160;sec (Harvard, 1940)</li>
</ul>

<p><b>a.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_anone"><a href="#ref_anone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Yale raced their 3V8 in this event.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Combination_race">Combination race</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Combination race">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Begun in 1920,<sup id="cite_ref-150yrs_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150yrs-22">[22]</a></sup> the combination boat is manned by rowers from the third varsity and second freshman boats, the strongest substitutes available to the junior varsity and freshman boats.</p>
<ul>
<li>Number of wins: Harvard, 15; Yale, 4</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Harvard%E2%80%93Yale_Regatta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; -webkit-column-width: 25em; column-width: 25em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1871data-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1871data_23-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The first regatta of the Rowing Association of American Colleges was held July 21, 1871, at Ingleside, Massachusetts, on the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_River" title="Connecticut River">Connecticut River</a>. <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Agricultural_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Massachusetts Agricultural College">Massachusetts Agricultural College</a> won the university race with Harvard second and <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a> third. Yale did not participate (nor join the RAAC) but continued to dispute its disqualification in the 1870 race with Harvard.<br />
"Record of the College Regattas: From the Winnipeseogee Contest in 1852 to that of Yesterday". <i>The New York Times</i>. July 15, 1875.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1872data-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1872data_24-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the RAAC university race of 1872, Harvard finished second and Yale sixth among six entries. <a href="/wiki/Amherst_College" title="Amherst College">Amherst College</a> won in 16:32.8 or 24.2 seconds ahead of Harvard. The crew generally rowed 40 to 46 strokes per minute.<br />
"The College Regatta: A Victory for Amherst. Another Surprise—Amherst the winners in 16:32 4-5, the best time on record ...". <i>New York Tribune</i>. July 25, 1872. p. 1.<br />
According to <i>The New York Times</i>, "A very strong current and quite a fresh breeze helped them along".</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1873data-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1873data_25-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the RAAC university race of 1873, Yale was finally declared the winner and the other places were not declared. "Shortly before midnight the referee announced that he would only decide upon the first position for the time being, and Yale he declared the winner of the race. The decision on other positions are reserved for a future time. Capt. Babcock, the referee, has stated to the Harvard boys that he is compelled technically, to award the University race to Yale, but he stated that the flags were not correctly placed at the finish, and that, consequently, the course on the east shore was much greater than on the west shore. The Harvards claim that the champion flags were awarded to them by the judges, whose judgment, like that of many others, was that Harvard had arrived at the finish in advance of all the crews ..."<br />
"Referee's Decision: Yale to take the Championship Colors". <i>Boston Daily Globe</i>. July 18, 1873.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1874data-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1874data_26-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">After two days of postponements a much diminished crowd watched the university race of the RAAC Regatta at Saratoga in 1874. Columbia won the race (unofficial time 16:42) officially followed by Wesleyan, Harvard, and six others, finally Yale. "It was unanimously acknowledged that Yale had the lead and Harvard second.Harvard's boat then ran into the Yale boat, breaking the latters' rudder."<br />
<i>San Francisco Chronicle</i> evidently quoting multiple accounts in <i>New York Evening Post</i></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1875data-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1875data_27-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the RAAC university race of 1875, Harvard finished third and Yale fifth among thirteen boats. Cornell won the race. Yale had been the betting favorite with Cornell second.<br />
"The News in this City: Intense Excitement Throughout New-York". <i>The New York Times</i>. July 15, 1875. p. 2.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1876debut-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1876debut_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The 1876 Harvard–Yale race introduced both the eight-oar crews with coxswain and the 4-mile distance, two features borrowed from the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_and_Cambridge_Boat_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford and Cambridge Boat Race">Oxford and Cambridge Boat Race</a>.<br />
Peter Mallory. <i>The Sport of Rowing: Two Centuries of Competition</i>. Four volumes. Henley-on-Thames, England: River Rowing Museum. 2011. Selections published online in advance as <i>row2k.com</i> Exclusive Features.</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">"Bob Cook: Pilgrimage to Britain – The Bob Cook Stroke". Mallory (2011), vol. 2, ch. 27 (pp. 312–18).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">"American Collegiate Rowing Takes Shape: Harvard versus Yale – The IRA". Mallory (2011), vol. 2, ch. 28 (pp. 319–29).</span></li>
</ul>
<span class="reference-text">Both featured online by <i>row2k.com</i> in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.row2k.com/content/MalloryCh2735.pdf">(Mallory, chapters 27–35)</a> (pages 312–60). Retrieved 2013-05-11.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1876RAAC-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1876RAAC_29-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Yale defeated Harvard soundly in a race of eight-oared boats in Springfield on June 30. Harvard continued west to Saratoga for the RAAC Regatta ("the Harvard six", for the Association championship matched "coxless sixes") but Yale did not participate. Harvard did not participate again and the Association disintegrated during the next several years. Regarding the Saratoga and Springfield events: "Yale does not row there, and Harvard will not after this year, but the eight-oared bout between Yale and Harvard, so successfully inaugurated to-day, will undoubtedly become an annual and permanent institution."<br />
"College Regatta: Yale and Harvard Eight-Oar Crews Try Conclusions. The Contest Takes Place on the Old Connecticut River Course." <i>Chicago Daily Tribune</i>. July 1, 1876. p. 8.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1903data-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1903data_30-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Two sources report time 20:19.6 for Harvard, different but greater times 20:19.8 and 20:29.8 for Yale, and Yale the winner.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-1952anniversary-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1952anniversary_31-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Following the race in New London in June, the schools held an exhibition in August on Lake Winnipesaukee to celebrate the 100th anniversary of the first regatta. The race followed the original script, with Harvard winning by 2.7 seconds.<br />
<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thecrimson.com/article/1952/2/8/harvard-yale-to-race-exhibition-in/">"Harvard, Yale to Race Exhibition in August; Practice Starts Today"</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gocrimson.com/sports/mcrew-hw/tradition/harvard-yale-regatta">"Harvard–Yale Regatta – 150 Years of Tradition"</a>.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
